Discussion of Results

The data comprised of 9551 restaurants dispersed across 141 cities and 1208 localities. Geographical 
analysis proved that the presence of restaurants was quite clustered in nature, with New Delhi representing
 more than 50 percent of total restaurants in the dataset. Other cities having the second and third highest number
  of restaurants were Gurgaon and Noida respectively.

Based on the location analysis, it can be stated that there were variations in restaurant ratings between
 cities and localities. There were some cities where restaurants had very high average ratings, namely London,
  Dubai, Bangalore, Hyderabad, and Chennai. Location analysis also helped in identifying variation in distribution 
  of restaurant densities, price ranges, and customer ratings based on geographical zones.

Analysis of latitude and longitude of restaurants proved that there were restaurants in different countries 
and different geographical zones. The results prove the importance of location in determining restaurant distribution
 and their customer ratings. Regions where there were many restaurants available were offering great choice to customers
  in terms of food type and prices.

Geographical analysis was used effectively to identify key areas with respect to restaurant concentration, 
highest customer ratings, and other geographical patterns in the dataset through city names, locality
